A photograph of Aidan de Brune taken in 1921.

I. — INTRODUCTION

On 20 September 1921 Aidan de Brune, a pseudonym of Herbert Charles Cull, set out from Sydney to walk around the perimeter of Australia in twelve months. As he described it:—

"To leave Sydney on foot, to walk ten thousand miles (more or less) around Australia, calling at all the ports en route on the four coasts, and to return to Sydney, was the task set me."

In the event, de Brune took two and a half years to complete the walk. He was laid up in Burketown Hospital in the Gulf Country of north western Queensland for about two months, in February and March 1922, and at other times did not walk, because of illness or because he chose to remain in a town and give a lecture on his travels. He was away from Sydney for 897 days, of which he walked on 572 days.

In October 1923, de Brune was near Ceduna, along the Great Australian Bight, on his way back to Sydney, with about 1500 miles to walk. A journalist, J. T. Beckett, who had met de Brune in Darwin, during the walk, wrote in The Northern Standard, Darwin:—

When you see him you want to get away from him. When you speak to him you don't want him to go away from you. He is a man and a gentleman up and down, and a library of information. He is a sport among sportsmen and a man of whom the Australian Journalists' Association should be proud, for he has not spared himself to get copy. Aiden de Brune has not finished his walk but should he never move another yard further, he will have put up a record that few, if any, will ever attempt to equal.

A biography of Aidan de Brune and a brief bibliography of his writings can be found in The Amateur Tramp by Colin Choat, available from Project Gutenberg Australia


II. — THE MANUSCRIPT DIARY

This ebook was made from Record Diary of a Walk Around Australia, a typescript created from de Brune's travelling diary, or manuscript diary. The diary consists of 4 notebooks.

Book 1 measures 2½in. x 4½inches (60mm. x 115mm.) and contains about 100 ruled pages. It covers the period 20 September 1921 to 12 May 1922

Books 2, 3 and 4 each measure 3 in. x 7 in. (75mm x 180mm.) and contain about 250 ruled pages.

Book 2 covers the period 13 May 1922 to 20 May 1923

Book 3 covers the period 21 May 1923 to 22 December 1923

Book 4 covers the period 23 December 1923 to end of the walk (4 March 1924).

Entries for each day have been neatly written up and contain details of the distance walked each day, together with the cumulative distance walked to the end of the day. Often there are entries made by people whom de Brune met at his destination, or along the way, certifying that he was at the place stated, on the stated day. Sometimes the people making the certification added well-wishes and other comments.


III. — THE TYPESCRIPT VERSION OF THE DIARY

Aidan de Brune converted his travelling diary, or manuscript journal, into a typescript book titled Record Diary of a Walk Around Australia, the basis of this ebook. A copy of the book is held by the State Library of New South Wales. The book consists of typed foolscap pages, bound in a maroon cover, with gold lettering on the spine. A hand-written note, on the title page of the book states:

"The original manuscript journal in four small pocket books is in the MSS. room of the Mitchell Library. Oct. 1924."

The next page of the book (unnumbered), contains the heading for the commencing section of the walk (i.e. New South Wales). It has a vertical hand-written, note down the left side of the page, which states:

"Don. Aidan de Brune 25/10/24"

Following the title page and the unnumbered "section" page, are 176 typed pages, together with 6 unnumbered pages, indicating the start of each subsequent section of the walk: Queensland, Northern Territory, Western Australia, South Australia, Victoria, and New South Wales. In this ebook details of the distances walked in each section are set out in the Statistics chapter.


IV. — RECORD DIARY OF A WALK AROUND AUSTRALIA

The typescript of the diary follows the order in which entries were made in the manuscript diary. In this ebook, a transcript of the typescript, a consistent format has been used for each day, showing, where present, the date; day number and diary day number; state or territory in which he was walking; cumulative days walked; daily distance (miles); cumulative distance; town/locality visited; note; certification/Comment.

De Brune made an entry in his diary for every day he was on his walk (897 days). He did not number the first day, on which he started out in mid-afternoon, probably because he did not get out of the Sydney Metropolitan area. Thereafter he numbered every day and, after some time, began also recording the number of days on which he actually walked (568).

Sometimes he did not walk because of bad weather, because he was ill, or because he wished to rest. Along the way he sometimes made minor errors in the day number. Then, towards the end of his walk, he obviously realised that that his day numbers did not tally with the actual number of days (897), although he had an entry for every day, showing the date. So he renumbered the final days. In this ebook, the day number first shown is the sequential day, starting from 1 and ending at 897. The Diary day Number is then shown afterwards, in square brackets.

PLACE NAMES

We cannot be certain that the places de Brune passed through will still be present on our modern maps, so it is sometimes not possible to plot the exact course which de Brune took. However, most of the places mentioned in the diary still exist today and by plotting some of the major towns through which he passed we are able to get a good idea of the track which he followed. In the outback, it is more difficult to plot his course. He often followed stock routes, which had bores with windmills attached, to obtain water for stock and humans; or railway lines which had bores with windmills to provide water for the steam locomotives. He also walked through the outback cattle stations, many of which, do not now exist, at least under the names by which de Brune identified them.

PUNCTUATION AND SPELLING

In the typescript version of the diary, de Brune was inconsistent in his capitalisation, his use of quotation marks and his spelling of place names, which he may have heard, but had not seen written down. The modern spelling of place names has been adopted in this ebook as well as a consistent approach to capitalisation and the use of quotes.

On nine occasions in the text, de Brune uses the word zump. It seems that this was an incorrect spelling of sump, defined by the Macquarie Dictionary as either "a pit, well, or the like in which water or other liquid is collected," or "a muddy pool or bog." Zump has been silently corrected to sump in the text.

DISTANCES

De Brune was as accurate as he could be with distances. In many cases he had to use his best guess to calculate the distance travlled in a day. No doubt he was careful to check his distances with the overall distance between points, which he found on sign posts, along railways lines and telegraph lines, or on maps.

Whatever the distance he travelled, his was an epic walk. Let us not be churlish in allowing him to describe it as a walk of "ten thousand miles."


De Brune's Route — Sydney to Sydney — Anticlockwise.

V. — NEW SOUTH WALES (NORTHERN SECTION)

20 September 1921
Day 1 [0]
State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 0
Daily Distance (miles): 12
Cumulative Distance (miles): 12
Town/Locality Visited: Sydney, Burwood, Rhodes, Meadowbank, Eastwood, Epping
Note: Walked out of Sydney and about 1½ miles from Burwood went on with Jimmy Brand of the Clyde Engineering Co. Thence to Rhodes and took track* over Parramatta River to Meadowbank. Thence to Eastwood and Epping where failed to cross railway and got bushed. Camped out. [de Brune did not count this as day 1. Ed.]
[* track=railway track on bridge spanning Parramatta River]
Certification/Comment: Aidan de Brune's trek around Australia in twelve months. This is to certify that bearer left the office of the Daily Mail Sydney at 3.45 p.m. on Tuesday 20 September 1921, (Signed) Jno. J. Gay (J.P.), Manager, Daily Mail.
21 September 1921
Day 2 [1]
State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 1
Daily Distance (miles): 25
Cumulative Distance (miles): 37
Town/Locality Visited: Hornsby, Asquith, Mount Colah, Kuring-gai, Berowra, Cowan
Note: The three roads. On to Hornsby. Arrived Hornsby 10.10 a.m. Left Hornsby 11 a.m. to Asquith and Mt. Colah (669 ft. above sea level.) About a mile past station and 100 yards off left side of road a black disc on stones marking highest point of Mt. Colah. Thence to Kuring-gai (702 ft. above sea level—a rise of 33 ft. in a mile.) Thence to Berowra, 27 miles, and rested, then on to Cowan to edge of hill overlooking Hawkesbury River, and camped. (Note views along hills and from Mt. Colah and summit marks.)
Certification/Comment: Arrived Hornsby at 10.10 a.m. (Signed) R.C. Tweedie, Hornsby Star.
22 September 1921
Day 3 [2]
State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 2
Daily Distance (miles): 24
Cumulative Distance (miles): 61
Town/Locality Visited: Hawkesbury River, Wondabyne, Woy Woy, Tascott, Point Clare, Gosford, Lisarow, Ourimbah, Wyong
Note: At Dawn descended by bad track to Hawkesbury River and walked across on railway—beautiful views. Wondabyne half-way over. Then through tunnel about mile long to Woy Woy, 45 miles. About two miles past, the monument to JACOBO GUTTER, MXCX? Then via Tascott, 4 miles, and Pt. Clare, 5 miles, to Gosford. Arrived Gosford 2 p.m. (3 miles outside Gosford the sign post moved to a new road, not necessary.) Thence to Lisarow (great orange show from here to Gosford). Thence to Ourimbah and camped out about 2 miles from Wyong.
Certification/Comment: Arrived Gosford, 2 p.m. E. J. Phillips, c/o Gosford Times.
23 September 1921
Day 4 [3]
State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 3
Daily Distance (miles): 33
Cumulative Distance (miles): 94
Town/Locality Visited: Catherine Hill Bay, Middle Camp, Main Camp, Swansea, Belmont
Note: Started before dawn. To Wyong, 2 miles. About 3 miles past Wyong called at farm for drink and well-entertained—English people. Then to Catherine Hill Bay, Middle Camp and Main Camp to Swansea.—where had only meal of day. Thence to Belmont and Camped.
Certification/Comment: Arrived Swansea, Lake Macquarie, 5.45 p.m. 23/9/21. (Signed) E. Masters, Swansea.
24 September 1921
Day 5 [4]
State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 4
Daily Distance (miles): 19
Cumulative Distance (miles): 113
Town/Locality Visited: Charlestown, Adamstown, Hamilton, Newcastle
Note: On at daybreak to Charlestown, 5 miles. To Adamstown, 9 miles—steam trams—to Hamilton and Newcastle. Left at 11 a.m. and on 9 miles towards West Maitland and camped.
Certification/Comment: Arrived Newcastle, 10 a.m., Saturday 24/9/21. Newcastle Herald per E. J. Thompson
25 September 1921
Day 6 [5]
State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 5
Daily Distance (miles): 27
Cumulative Distance (miles): 140
Town/Locality Visited: West Maitland, Lochinvar, Greta, Branxton
Note: On at dawn to Maitland, 6 miles, through West Maitland. Thence through Lochinvar and Greta to Branxton. Then on 4 miles and camped.
26 September 1921
Day 7 [6]
State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 6
Daily Distance (miles): 31
Cumulative Distance (miles): 171
Town/Locality Visited: Whittingham, Singleton, Rixs Creek, Glennies Creek, Ravensworth, Antiene
Note: On at dawn and 5 miles on, signpost "Watch the bridge." Why? On to Whittingham , 9 miles, thence to Singleton, 12 miles. (Mrs McGregor and 4 children.) Thence to Rixs Creek, 4 miles. To Glennies Creek, 8 miles. To Ravensworth, 12 miles. To Antiene, 18 miles, and 2 miles on to camp.
Certification/Comment: Arrived Singleton 10.05 a.m. leaving few minutes later. (Signed) J. S. North C/o Argus.
27 September 1921

State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 7
Daily Distance (miles): 34
Cumulative Distance (miles): 205
Town/Locality Visited: Muswellbrook, Aberdeen, Scone
Note: On at daybreak to Muswellbrook. Thence to Aberdeen, 8 miles. To Scone, 8 miles. Thence 8 miles on road to Murrurundi
Certification/Comment: Arrived Muswellbrook at 9.50 a.m. 27/9/21, (Signed) R. E. McClintock, for the Muswellbrook Chronicle.
28 September 1921
Day 9 [8]
State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 8
Daily Distance (miles): 26
Cumulative Distance (miles): 231
Town/Locality Visited: Wingen, Murrurundi, Ardglen
Note: On foot at daybreak. To Wingen, 2 miles, then met five hobos. "Singing Bill." About 5 miles from Murrurundi is steep hill. Over crest is monument to Peter Clark who was killed by Wilson, the bushranger, while trying to arrest him. Magnificent views over hills, to-day and yesterday. Thence to Murrurundi, 13 miles. Thence to Ardglen, 6 miles, and 4 miles on and camped.
Certification/Comment: Arrived Murrurundi 28/9/21 2.30 p.m. (Signed) S. Wright, post office. Wishing good luck.

Cumulative Distance (miles): 248
Town/Locality Visited: Willow Tree
Note: On at dawn to Willow Tree, (Girls in motor camping out), 4 miles. Thence within 4 miles of Wallabadah, and camped at Chris Foster's, owing to creek flooding.

Passed two travellers going south 10 miles north of Tamworth. To Moonbee, 8½ miles, and then to 302-mile mark. On to 327-mile mark and camped.
Certification/Comment: Arrived Tamworth, 10.10 a.m. 5/10/21, The Northern Daily Leader, (Signed) A. Joseph, Managing Director.

Certification/Comment: Arrived Bendemeer 10.40 am 6/10/21. (Signed) G. B. Hewitt, postmaster.

Town/Locality Visited: Black Mountain
Note: Left Mr Burgess at 7.30 a.m. and in to town of Armidale. Left shortly after, for Glen Innes. Took east road by mistake and had to return. Dinner at farmer's. Left Armidale about 1 p.m. Saw first black—a gin with 2 children about 1 mile out of Armidale. On to Black Mountain.
Certification/Comment: Arrived Armidale 10.15 a.m. 11/10/21, (Signed) J. McKenzie, Part Proprietor, Armidale Express. Arrived at "Sunnyside" at 9 p.m. Black Mountain. (Signed) W. J. McLean 11/10/21.

Cumulative Days Walked: 16
Daily Distance (miles): 30
Cumulative Distance (miles): 404
Town/Locality Visited: Guyra, Llangothlin
Note: Left before sunrise for Guyra, 7 miles. A mile from Guyra passed traveller—old man, deaf as post. Just outside Guyra met a man who asked "Have you a 6d." "Why?" "I'd like a drink." On to Llangothlin. Road bad after Guyra. To 15-mile mark.
Certification/Comment: Arrived at Guyra 12/10/21. (Signed) Frank J. Mann, Argus Office, Guyra. Arrived at Llangothlin 12/10/21 12 noon. (Signed) L. Birtle, Store, Llangothlin.

Cumulative Distance (miles): 453
Town/Locality Visited: Glencoe, Stonehenge, Glen Innes
Note: Started at sunrise. On to Glencoe. Two miles out of Glencoe met traveller and at 10½ miles met traveller with swag on wheel-barrow. To Stonehenge, 7 miles. Last mile of road to Stonehenge station awful. To Glen Innes, 7 miles. Then on to 25-mile mark.
Certification/Comment: Arrived Glencoe 6.30 a.m. 13/10/21 (Signed) A Dobbs, Store, Glencoe. Arrived Glen Innes 2 p.m. 13/10/21 (Signed) Clive Harrison, Glen Innes Guardian.
14 October 1921
Day 25 [24]
State or Territory: NSW-North
Cumulative Days Walked: 18
Daily Distance (miles): 28
Cumulative Distance (miles): 481
Town/Locality Visited: Bolivia Pass, Bolivia, Bluff Rock, Bungulla, Tenterfield
Note: Started at sunrise. To top of Bolivia pass (3250 ft.). Down to Bolivia, 6miles. Held up by storm for 2 hours. Scenes on hills as of vast forest fires (clouds). Passed traveller at Bolivia, another 2 miles out, and yet another at 4 miles, all going south. Fine bridge across river 10½ miles south of Tenterfield. To Bluff Rock 5 miles. To Bungulla, 3 miles (3150 ft.). To Tenterfield. On 3 miles. Terrific storm in night. Wonderful lightning.
Certification/Comment: Tenterfield, 5 p.m. 14/10/21, (Signed) E. G. Waddell, The Star.

VI. — QUEENSLAND

Note: [Entered Queensland. Ed.] Started late. To Sunnyside, 6miles. (Hobos on road.) To Wallangarra and Queensland border, 5 miles. On to Bald Mountain, 3 miles. To Wyberba, 4 miles. To Lyra, 2 miles. To Ballandean, 3 miles. To Glen Alpin, 7 miles. To Beverley, 2 miles, where camped. Fine day. Today met again Mickie White, a young sailor.
Certification/Comment: Arrived Wallangarra 11 a.m. 15/10/21, (Signed) E. Taylor, for S.M. Wallangarra.

End of month—611 miles being 89 miles short on schedule.

[There is confusion here. The total at end of day 63 was 1347 miles. No distance recorded until end of day 67, when it was 1417 miles. Hampden to Proserpine is 60 miles per "Google" map, so he wasn't far out in his recording. Ed.]

22 March 1922
Day 184 [183]
State or Territory: QLD
Cumulative Days Walked: 125
Daily Distance (miles): 0
Cumulative Distance (miles): 2518
Town/Locality Visited: Albert River, Punjaub Swamp
Note: Left hospital at 9 a.m. and Burketown at 9:30 a.m. Took lower road, 2 miles out of town, saving some miles. Met a Mr King carting down to Camooweal way. About 11 went to Albert River and camped until about 4 p.m. Very hot. I am very soft and heat beats me. Feet poor. About sunset caught up to Booth and had cup of tea. Then, on to the pool (1 mile) and by Punjaub swamp, to the Hut, arriving there about midnight. Camped on Verandah.
23 March 1922
Day 185 [184]
State or Territory: QLD
Cumulative Days Walked: 126
Daily Distance (miles): Not Recorded.
Cumulative Distance (miles): 2518
Note: Found Shackleton [was] away from hut. (A traveller there, old man, very shaky.) Ate nothing yesterday and a slice of bread for this breakfast. Then, on to the ruins at Brookdale Hotel and onto the Punjaub Road. About 11, heat overwhelming and went across paddock to water. About 8 miles out. Then on through night to try to reach Punjaub. Mosquitoes very bad last night and today. Arrived at rabbit-proof gate about midnight and camped.
24 March 1922
Day 186 [185]

Daily Distance (miles): Not Recorded.
Cumulative Distance (miles): 2518
Town/Locality Visited: Punjaub Station
Note: Crossed 12-mile creek and on to Punjaub fence and over swamp. Heat, flies and mosquitoes very bad. Touch of fever and feet very painful.
25 March 1922

Day 190 [189]
State or Territory: QLD
Cumulative Days Walked: 129
Daily Distance (miles): Not Recorded.
Cumulative Distance (miles): 2563
Note: Left Punjaub early. Road very bad. Took 60-mile road as believed better watered. Road very cut up. Black Soil. Walk at night in bush (experiment). Found water in morning to westward. Very hot, no wind, mosquitos and flies bad.
[Recorded this day correctly as Tuesday 28/3/22. Also incorrectly gave next day same date. Ed.]
29 March 1922
Day 191 [190/191]
State or Territory: QLD
Cumulative Days Walked: 130/131
Daily Distance (miles): Not Recorded.
Cumulative Distance (miles): 2563
Town/Locality Visited: Lawn Hill Creek
Note: Road improved after first ten miles from Punjaub and fair pad along. Found Lawn Hill Creek, a nice running stream. Country fairly well wooded but little black soil. Saw no one. Plenty water. Creek close by and swamps. Mosquitos terrific at camp and flies bad. Very hot. Feet improving. Later: Mosquitos bad. Feet much better. Country better wooded and water abundant. Very hot day. Did a fair distance. Saw no one. Very little stock.
[Recorded day incorrectly as Wednesday 28/3/22 and again as Thursday 28/3/22. Day of week corrected at day 243, but he has inadvertently added a day to his total days. Ed.]
30 March 1922
Day 192 [192]
State or Territory: QLD
Cumulative Days Walked: 132
Daily Distance (miles): Not Recorded.
Cumulative Distance (miles): 2563
Note: Cooler morning. Road not so good. Much bush and good red soil. Hills on each side of distance. Camped midday by double pools. Very hot. On to boundary rider's hut, 18 miles from Lawn Hill Station.
31 March 1922

01 April 1922
Day 194 [194]

Day 292 [292]
State or Territory: NT
Cumulative Days Walked: 172
Daily Distance (miles): 18
Cumulative Distance (miles): 3171
Note: On to Mill Bore No. 6.
Met Director of Works, N.T. 6 miles north of Frew's Ponds and he gave me the following mileage which will be adopted as official:
Frew Ponds to No 6 (Milner), 18 miles. To No 5 (McGowry), 18 miles. To Daly waters, 13 miles. To No 4 (Rodericks), 12 miles. To No. 3 (Ironstone), 18 miles. To No. 2, 18 miles. To No. 1, 18 miles. To Warlock Ponds, 27 miles. To Bitter Springs, 14 miles. (Bitter Springs to Mataranka, off road, 3 miles.) To Marranboy, 40 miles. To Katherine, 38 miles. Total, 234 miles.
Came down Jump-up and across 3 miles. Black soil plain.
Camped about 200 yards south of bore, not seeing it in dark.
Certification/Comment: Percy J. Mooney 8 July 1922.
09 July 1922
Day 293 [293]

Daily Distance (miles): 18
Cumulative Distance (miles): 3189

10 July 1922
Day 294 [294]
State or Territory: NT
Cumulative Days Walked: 174
Daily Distance (miles): 12
Cumulative Distance (miles): 3201
Town/Locality Visited: Daly Waters
Note: On to Daly Waters Telegraph Station. Mill at No. 5 not working. Met Administrator and party (five), about 4 miles from Mill No. 5. Did not stop. Telegraph line again came in about 2 miles on and ran along road to within 3½ miles of Daly Waters. Then, after turning off at waterhole, came to line. Then to Daly Waters Telegraph Station.
Certification/Comment: T. C. Urquhart, Administrator, N.T.
Mr de Brune arrived at Daly Waters Telegraph Station 10/7/22. (Signed) W. Holtz.

I dreamed last night to heaven I did go/Where did you come from they wanted to know/And when I said "Broome," Oh didn't they stare/Walk right in. You're the first one from there. J. Hillard, Broome.
Wishing every success to a plucky sport, on a dangerous and trying journey. F. Beaumont.
W. H. Graves.
At the request of several Broome residents Mr Aidan de Brune delivered an address to a gathering assembled at the Star Hotel, on the evening of the 25th December, giving his experience of the journey, on foot, from Sydney to Broome. The address was very interesting and much appreciated and Mr de Brune was given best wishes for the safe and successful completion of his undertaking, and 3 cheers for what he had already done. George Moss, Chairman of Meeting.
A well-wisher of Mr A. de Brune. J. Nilssan.
Bravery has its reward. R. Hornsby, Broome. 26/12/22.
Good luck. (Miss) A. King, Broome.
Many people see nothing in anything which does not lead to personal aggrandisement. But it is to such men as Mr Aidan de Brune that we owe the present position and power of the British Empire. Without men of the spirit of adventure where would our Empire have been today? The worst part of his travels, I believe, has been accomplished, and my wish is that he will successfully win through, to the gratification, at least of...H. D. Forbes 26/12/22.

25 January 1923
Day 493 [486]
State or Territory: WA
Cumulative Days Walked: 303
Daily Distance (miles): 20
Cumulative Distance (miles): 5514
Town/Locality Visited: Strelley station
Note: On to Strelley Station, 8 miles.
Arrived at Strelley station at 10.30. Went to homestead. Manager came out and asked how I dare come on verandah. When I gave my name he said he had heard of me and told me he would come out later. He came out after a while but did not come to me. Presently Chinese cook came to me with some tucker wrapped in paper.
To Pundano, 12 miles.
Certification/Comment: Mr A. de Brune arrived last night. Pleased to meet so interesting and entertaining a gentleman. He is going strong on his great walking stunt—Henry E. Bell.

The staff of the Union Bank, Roebourne, heartily welcome Mr A. de Brune on his Australian Tour. We trust he will disclose the numerous privileges attained by residing in Roebourne!!! We wish him every success. E. Mills, 5/2/23.
Mr A. de Brune arrived at Roebourne in a vehicle commonly known as per boot, probably the nearest approach to travelling by Ford car—I being the proud owner of one. He seemed to be suffering from gear box trouble, which was immediately attended to in order that he might proceed on his tireless journey. I wish him every success—Frank Porter, Jubilee Hotel, Roebourne, 5/2/23.
Every wish for a successful tour and a safe return to Sydney. O. E. Healey, 5/2/23.
George Fisher. Met Mr A. de Brune, Roebourne, 4/2/23.
Roebourne, 6/2/23. Mr A. de Brune called in, looking well after his long walk.—H. G. Creagh, postmaster, 6/2/23.
Life is mostly froth and bubble/Two things stand alone/Kindness in another's trouble/Courage in your own.
Le Brune has the courage of 100 men to take on a lone hand through country infested with blacks, dry tracks, and the seven plagues of Egypt combined.
Best of wishes to A. de Brune who has the heart of a lion and the pluck of the good old Bull Dog breed, to carry on. He has my sympathy, humping Matilda, under present climatic conditions. He is a good ad. for the White Australia Policy. He is also a walking encyclopedia on Australia and things Australian. One reward he should have, should be a snug billet at Australia House, Strand. Billy Hughes please note this.—Alfred E. Neaves. Roebourne, 6/2/23.
I wish you astonishing luck. I. Mandrell, M.O., R.M.
On behalf of the residents of Roebourne, I welcome Mr de Brune to this district. He is giving a lecture this evening on his travels, which will be most interesting to the residents. He arrived looking very fit after his long walk, and we wish him a safe journey and happy ending to a very long trip. Tom Stove, Chairman, Roebourne Roads Board, 5/2/23.
Wishing Mr de Brune a good trip and a safe return to Sydney. (Miss) Lily Porter, Roebourne.
Kate Bateman. Bon Voyage.
I have found Mr Aidan de Brune very interesting in the account of his varied experiences and many adventures on his long walking tour and I wish him every success and a safe return to his headquarters in Sydney. A. L. Bickerton.

Mr de Brune, after one day's "pink-eye" (holiday) made a bee line for Onslow (120 miles) per "shinner" (foot). "Minnawarra" (by-and-by) he "catchem" Sydney, but "struth" what a long way to walk. Reg. Blinks "galloping bedstead" (Ford) more better. Good bye, good luck.—J. J. Taylor, postmaster, Fortescue. 13/2/23.

The machine is claimed to be the latest model—built on streamline body, never known to nose dive or side slip, guaranteed reliable. I wish him the best of luck and a safe return. H. Tozer.

Day 518 [510]
State or Territory: WA
Cumulative Days Walked: 322
Daily Distance (miles): 27
Cumulative Distance (miles): 5881
Town/Locality Visited: Onslow
Note: To Onslow per above table (day 507), 27 miles.
Certification/Comment: Ashburton Hotel, Onslow, 19/2/23. Mr de Brune arrived here at 7.30 p.m. per Irish tandem. Looks well and fit having covered 27 miles today, making a total to date of 5881 miles. Mr de Brune is most interesting to converse with, as his knowledge of other countries is so large and varied and his unique knowledge of continent, acquired first hand, is most valuable. We wish him a successful finish to his tour, and hope his reward will be in line with his effort. Frederick J Lapthorn.
20.2.23. Onslow. Norman Brearley. Airways Ltd.
Mr A. de Brune called at Police Station, Onslow on 20/2/23. He reported feeling fit and well on his walk around Australia. I wish him good luck. M. F. Pilkington, Const. 1033.
Mr A. de Brune called at Onslow post office 20/2/23. Temperature 110.2 [degrees fahrenheit. Ed.]. Wrote his telegram outside the office. Thought he was in Hades. We admire his courage and fortitude in facing the arduous task of walking around Australia, and wish him every success. Jas. J. Coles, postmaster. [Did de Brune or the postmaster think that de Brune was in Hades?]
Best wishes for a successful trip, old chap. J. Beecroft.
Onslow, 19/2/23. Mr A. de Brune called on me at Onslow on the above date, looking as brown and well as a real bushman. We wish him every success in his arduous task, and a real bumper day when he reaches his office in Sydney. Onslow Clark.
Arthur E. Stenning, R. M. Onslow. 20/2/23.

Town/Locality Visited: Horse Works Mill
Note: Went on 6 miles on out road and then took track which bent eastwards, and after full day's walk landed at Horse Works Mill—well away from my route. About 25 miles.
Certification/Comment: 25/2/23. Mr de Brune arrived at our camp at Horse Works at sundown, having lost his way. He is on a trip round Australia per boot. Mr de Brune is perfectly sane and normal on every other subject and I feel quite sure his trip will effect a perfect cure. Good luck and a happy ending to his trip. C. R. Smith, Globe Hill, near Onslow.

Cumulative Distance (miles): 6720
Town/Locality Visited: Walebing

Certification/Comment: T. Crowley, postmaster. Received packet of letters from Moora.
Walebing, 6/6/23. To wish you success and good health for the remainder of your long journey to Sydney. (Lady) Madeline E. S. Lefroy.
Mr Aidan de Brune reached my home on his great walk round Australia at six o'clock this evening and we have spent an interesting time with him. My best wishes go with him. (Sir) H. B. Lefroy, Walebing. 6/6/23.
07 June 1923
Day 626 [618]
State or Territory: WA
Cumulative Days Walked: 377
Daily Distance (miles): 18
Cumulative Distance (miles): 6738
Town/Locality Visited: New Norcia
Note: To New Norcia, 21 miles. but delayed by constant rains and only went 18 miles. from Walebing.
Certification/Comment: Old Victoria Plains Hotel, Waddington, 92 miles from Perth. Wishing you every success and good health in completing your long and trying task. A. C. Norwood.
Waterloo, 7/6/23. Had the pleasure of meeting Mr de Brune today on his long walk around Australia. He looks fit and well after his trying task and I wish him the best of health and luck on the remainder of his journey. P. J. Murphy, Waterloo.
Summer Hill, 7/6/23. To our surprise, today we had the pleasure of meeting Mr de Brune on his long weary walk around Australia. We wish him good luck and may God be with him until he returns to the end of his journey. (Mrs) J. Halligan, Summer Hill.
08 June 1923
Day 627 [619]
State or Territory: WA
Cumulative Days Walked: 378
Daily Distance (miles): 9
Cumulative Distance (miles): 6747
Note: Very bad rains and hail, all day, delayed walking. Went all over New Norcia Monastery and then on about 2 miles.
Certification/Comment: New Norcia, W.A., 7/6/23. While waiting for a hot cup of tea at New Norcia, Mr A. de Brune walked in. He told us of his undertaking and he is to be congratulated and admired, if successful. The weather here is awful. I find it bad enough getting about in my motor car. I wish you every success and a safe journey. B. L. Sergrant, Mt. Lawley, Perth.
Mr de Brune called at New Norcia on his long walking journey round Australia. May God crown his efforts with a full success. A. Catalan, O.S.B.* Abbot, Abbey of New Norcia, 8/6/23. [* Order of St. Benedictine. Ed.]
V. Ubach, O.S.B., Procurator of this Abbey.
Mr de Brune arrived here today accompanied by a shower of hail. That he may accomplish a task which only a man of stout heart would attempt, is the fervent wish of Mrs Lanigan and myself. Joseph P. Lanigan, R.M.
Had the pleasure of meeting Mr Aidan de Brune here today and he looked well and hearty, considering his long walk through difficult country, his description of which was very entertaining. Wishing Mr de Brune good health and strength to fulfil the great effort. R. P. Lanigan, J.P. New Norcia, 8/6/23.

Day 632 [624]
State or Territory: WA
Cumulative Days Walked: 383
Daily Distance (miles): 20
Cumulative Distance (miles): 6846
Town/Locality Visited: Midland Junction, Redcliffe, Belmont, Subiaco
Note: to Midland Junction, 5 miles. To Perth, via Redcliffe and Belmont, 12 miles. To Subiaco, 3 miles.
Certification/Comment: Mr de Brune called at Swan Express office on 13/6/23 at 8.35 a.m. Jas. W. Dawson.
Jno. Gerrans, postmaster, Midland Junction.
Guildford, 13/6/23. A good traveller and I wish him every success. M. J. Rawson.
Guildford, 13/6/23. Mr de Brune called here this day. Padbury's Stores Ltd, per A. Barton.
Mr de Brune presented himself at the Sunday Times Office, Stirling Street, Perth, W.A. 13/6/23. J. P. Fry, sub-editor.
Mr de Brune called at the Westralian Worker office 13/6/23. He talked of his experiences in the Territory and the Nor'-West, to my great advantage. I congratulate Australia on having renewed, in him, the splendid exploring qualities of the earliest of its investigators, and I do hope the people of the South will heed his counsel. John Curtin, editor.
We were delighted to welcome our old friend Aidan de Brune on his arrival in Perth today, on his long exciting and adventurous walk around Australia. We wish him the best of luck for the rest of his journey and hope it will not be long before we meet him again. Bon Voyage, old chap. 13/6/23. C. J. R. Le Mesurier, (Mrs) R. Le Mesurier.
13/6/23. Mr de Brune called at my office today. I am satisfied he has already accomplished a wonderful feat. I know the difficulties of the W.A. bush tracks. I wish him luck. H. Willington, Gen. Sec. A.L.P., Trades Hall, Perth.

Day 645 [637]

Cumulative Days Walked: 396
Daily Distance (miles): 14
Cumulative Distance (miles): 7035
Town/Locality Visited: Highbury, Nuralin Pool, Piesse

Certification/Comment: Arrived Highbury, Wednesday, 11 a.m. Z. A. Lee.
Mr A. de Brune called at Hillside, Nuralin Pool, on the afternoon of 26/6/23. on his walk round Australia. Although the weather is very wet Mr de Brune seems to be in the best of spirits, and going strong and well. With best wishes for the successful completion of his journey. S. F. de Lany.
Piesse, 26/6/23. On his walk round Australia Mr de Brune arrived at our home this evening. We persuaded him to stay the night and were delighted to hear a short lecture on his impressions gained during his long journey. We trust those in authority will put to good use the knowledge gained at first hand of our great north land by Mr de Brune—Norman S. Harvey, Rose M. Harvey.
Thomas Quinlan has met you at Barton, via Wagin, with Jerry O'Connor. Tuesday 26th June 1923.
Rogers, Esperance Railway.
Evelyn M. Tombs, who met Mr de Brune at Piesse, 26th June 1923. He has my best wishes for a successful finish to his journey.

Day 649 [641]

I met Mr de Brune at Tambellup, being away from home and staying in a railway sleeping van. He was pleased to have a warm at our fire. I wish him every success in his walk around Australia. Very pleased to have had a talk with him. A. Ashton, Katanning.
30th June, 1923. Isolated at Tambellup, owing to railway line being washed away, about 7 p.m. the bearer Mr de Brune announced his arrival. His diaries and conversation were very interesting, indeed. I wish him every success on his long walk. S. Scarborough, 30th/6/1923.
Met Mr de Brune and he don't like Billy Hughes. L Hanna.
Mr de Brune leaving Tambellup on his long arduous journey, Sunday morning, 1/7/23. F. W. Chandler, Constable, Tambellup, 30/6/23.

Plantagenet Road Board, Mt. Barker, 4/7/23. Called this day. E. W., Secretary.
Narrikup, 4/7/23. We had quite a surprise in seeing Mr de Brune and we wish him all the best of luck in his career. (Mrs) G. S. Elliott.
Narrikup, 4/7/23. Mr de Brune's experiences have been very interesting and I sincerely hope the water will be low and his spirits high for the remainder of his trip. (Miss) G. W. Rushton.

Albany, 9/7/23. Aidan de Brune, a blazer of the track in working class hopes in Australia. That the future will be kind to him and his is the very earnest wish of W. Mather, State Representative, Waterside Workers Federation of Australia and R. A. Pike, President, Albany Lumpers Union.
Albany, 8/7/23. Mr de Brune has a wonderful story to relate of his journeying around Australia's coastline. A keen observer and fluent speaker, his articles and lectures should do much to dispel the erroneous impressions possessed by many residents of the East regarding this State. Reginald Greenwood, Advertiser Office.
God speed you on the trip home. R. G. Mills, Albany, 13/7/23.

Mr Aidan de Brune, arrived at my house on Saturday 14/7/23, and I have had the pleasure of reading his diaries and have thereby renewed many old acquaintances and associations of my travels from Wyndham to Albany. I consider his feat in accomplishing what he has so far done is nothing short of marvellous, knowing the State as I do. I wish him God Speed and a safe journey for the remaining portion of his wonderful tour, and hope some day to renew my acquaintance with him. Ben J. Smith, Lower Kalgan, 15/7/23.

Cumulative Distance (miles): 7409
Town/Locality Visited: Hopetoun
Note: To Hopetoun, 18 miles.
Certification/Comment: Geo. Parsons, Riverlea Farm.
Mr de Brune reached Hopetoun 5 p.m. 25/7/23 en route Sydney. I take this opportunity of wishing him the best of luck on the final stage of his long journey around Australia. W. E. Parry, postmaster, Hopetoun.
Mr de Brune addressed an audience at Hopetoun, whom he delighted with stories of the experiences during his travels, and a hearty vote of thanks was accorded him and he was wished good luck, good health and a safe termination to his long, tiresome journey. Phillip E. Teague, chairman, Hopetoun. 25/7/23.
I have just had the pleasure of hearing Mr de Brune address a meeting at Hopetoun and cannot find words to express my appreciation of the clear and intellectual discourse and can only hope the resultant issue will meet with the success that he deserves and that it will be the means of awaking the people of Australia to the great possibilities of this great Commonwealth. H. Donovan. 25/7/23.
Hopetoun, 25/7/23. Mr de Brune, I am pleased to have met and conversed with you and was delighted with the highly interesting and instructive narrative of portion of your travel. I am glad to know that you have safely accomplished the greater part of your long tmamp and trust that Dame Fortune may be your conductress on the balance of your stroll, and that you may arrive at your terminal point in the best of health and spirits. Good luck! God be with you. (Mrs) E. V. Hiller.
Metropolitan Hotel, Hopetoun, W.A., 25/7/23. Spent a pleasant few hours listening to Mr de Brune's experiences. He seems to have passed some anxious times. We hope the latter part of his journey home to Sydney will be more pleasant, and will look forward to news of his arrival. He is staying at present with us, enjoying a rest. A. Hiller.
Hopetoun, 25/7/23. Wishing Mr de Brune every success on his homeward journey. (Miss) C. Halbert.
To wish Mr A. de Brune a very good wish on his journey to Sydney. Written by one who has been in the the Kimberleys for a short period. Long life and happiness. (Mrs) Myrtle Knox.
Delighted to have had the pleasure of hearing Mr A. de Brune lecture on his journey per foot around Australia, and trust he will successfully reach his home in Sydney. (Miss) H. B. Veal, 27/723, Hopetoun, Western Aust.
Hopetoun, 26/7/23. Mr de Brune—Dear sir, I herewith compliment you on the courage, endurance and success which has attended to your enterprise in your walk around Australia, and wish you every success to the terminal point. Thomas Veal.

Day 682 [673]
State or Territory: WA
Cumulative Days Walked: 423
Daily Distance (miles): 19
Cumulative Distance (miles): 7543
Note: On Towards Esperance. To. Mr Daw's Farm, 19 miles.
Certification/Comment: Moujebank, 2/8/23. When driving home, about six miles out of town (Esperance) we met Mr de Brune, with his swag up and walking very lame. We didn't know whom he was and took him for a sundowner at first. But he told us his name and we gladly escorted him back to our house for the night and spent a very pleasant evening in his company. The stories of his experiences, etc., his papers and diary were both wonderful and interesting. With best wishes and good luck for the remainder of his journey. Florence Daw, Fred C. Daw.

Esperance, 3/8/23. I have the honour to testify that Mr A. de Brune called on me and had an interesting talk. I was much interested in his mission, and he was in his turn interested in me as a resident of Esperance for 29 years. With best wishes to him, Yours, Thos. R. Orr.

Israelite Bay, 26/8/23. Mr de Brune arrived mid-day looking as fit as a fiddle and smiling. Having already tramped close on 8000 miles and still another 2000 to go. We wish him the very best of health and good fortune on the last stages of his long and wonderful tramp, and may he arrive in Sydney before Xmas 1923. W. Looney, postmaster, Israelite Bay.
Israelite Bay, 29/8/23. Wishing you a safe trip and very happy Xmas. (Mrs) V. Looney.
Israelite Bay, 29/8/23. I have had the pleasure of meeting Mr de Brune and of also reading his diary which contains names of friends in other parts. I wish him the best of good luck for the remainder of his long walk. (Mrs) S. Brown.
Israelite Bay, 29/8/23. Having had the pleasure of meeting Mr de Brune and speaking to him of other parts of the country than this with which he is acquainted I feel sure that his hard and wonderful task shall never be fully appreciated, other than by those who know the class of country he has travelled through and have had to depend on their own resources. Wishing him every success. W. T. Brown.
Pleased to have met Mr de Brune. J. Tait, Israelite Bay.

Day 718 [709]
State or Territory: WA
Cumulative Days Walked: 441
Daily Distance (miles): 24
Cumulative Distance (miles): 7899
Town/Locality Visited: Eyre
Note: To Eyre, 24 miles.
Certification/Comment: Eyre, South Coast, W.A., 9/9/23. Mr A. de Brune arrived here from Israelite Bay on the evening of the 7th, looking very well, after what must have been one of his worst stages. He has carried a message to me from Wyndham, a distance of nearly 4000 miles. I wish him very good luck during the remainder of his journey to Sydney. J. Simpson, postmaster, Eyre. W.A.
Eyre, 9/9/23. Had the pleasure of Mr de Brune's company for the evening and found him very interesting on his travels, on his long walk around Australia. He is looking well and hearty after his 7900 miles tramp. Also had a little talk on his experiences in other countries. I wish him everything that's good. I hope to hear of his safe arrival in Sydney. B. G. Hutchings.
Eyre, 9/9/23. Wishing Mr de Brune every success on his long journey on foot around Australia. Mrs C. M. Hutchings.
Mr de Brune may be a famous "Sydney Mail" pedestrian, but it strikes me he's a lady's man too. He loves his cups of tea. We have thoroughly enjoyed his stay with us. I thank him for bringing a message from Wyndham for Billie Pearce. Eyre, 10/9/23.
P.M.G. Line Party. Mr Aidan de Brune arrived at our camp. I wish him the best of luck on his long walk around Australia. This great walk, along with his valuable experience, together with his own education, should prove of great use to Australia, and he should be a very desirable person to meet on his arrival at Sydney. H. Garner, lineman, P.M.G. Dept.
The best of luck to Mr A. de Brune. (Mrs) E. M. Pearce, Eyre, 10/9/23.
Mr de Brune's heart must be as big as Australia to undertake such a task. Good luck to you from (Mrs) A. M. Simpson, Eyre, 10/9/23.

Fowler's Bay, 3/10/23. I have had very much pleasure in meeting Aidan de Brune who is walking around Australia. Mr de Brune, a kindred spirit. To him luck. Victor C. Williams, W. H. Betts Ltd, Fowler's Bay.
Mr de Brune arrived here today. We all find him very interesting and wish him every success on the rest of his journey to Sydney. E. W. Dolling, F. K. Dolling, (Miss) E. A. Dolling, J. W. Dolling, (Mrs) C. F. Dolling.

Day 747 [738]

Daily Distance (miles): 18
Cumulative Distance (miles): 8373
Town/Locality Visited: Charra
Note: On towards Ceduna (Murat Bay). To Charra, 18 miles.
Certification/Comment: Charra, 6/10/23. Mr Aidan de Brune arrived at my farm from Penong tonight looking fit and well and in good spirit. I had an interesting chat with him on his great experience, which should be helpful to many people seeking such information as Mr de Brune can give. My best wishes go with him, and may the feat which he has nearly accomplished be crowned with success, and his great enterprise be the means of paving the way for future people to advance and settle our great continent. Wishing good luck and good health to the end. Edgar T. Mewett.

G. P. Roberts.
Monseavu House, Petina, 16/10/23. Mr de Brune arrived here about sundown per (Cruick) shank's power. He gave Mr Roberts and self a most instructive and musical evening. May he reach his journey's end on time and in health. A. M. Mellor, of Glenelg, S.A.

Certification/Comment: Mr de Brune arrived here about mid-day bringing his total mileage to 8679 miles. I am looking forward with pleasure to an interesting hour or so with him this evening. His journey is nearly ended and I trust the remainder will be accomplished under the best of conditions. P. J. Brett, postmaster, 31/10/23.

9/11/23/ Wirrabarra, S.A. Whilst motoring north this afternoon and exchanging the usual courtesy to a pedestrian, making south, I remarked to my friend Mr Passow, "That's the Joker walking round Australia." I had occasion to find out later that there is many a true word spoken in jest when I met Mr A. de Brune at the Hotel, that evening, and passed with him a most pleasant time. J. F. Beckett.
J. E. Hanmill, postmaster, Wirrabara, S.A. 10/11/23.

His walk being from Sydney around Australia and back to Sydney.

Gladstone 14/11/23. It affords me great pleasure to have made the acquaintance of Mr de Brune on his overland tour. Mr de Brune, whilst at Gladstone, gave a very interesting address on his travels, of what he had seen and the wonderful resources of the Northern Territory. He takes with him my best wishes for a pleasant journey and safe return home. C. E. Wilson, Police Officer.
Gladstone, 14/11/23. I had the pleasure last night of hearing Mr de Brune lecture and was, with others, deeply interested. He has a wonderful story to tell and is able, by voice and pen, to reproduce the impressions gained on his long, lonely walk. I hope that his pluck and powers of endurance will take him safely through to the completions of his journey, and that the knowledge he has to impart will result, as it should do, in great and lasting benefit to the Commonwealth. W. Hancock, Areas Express.
Georgetown, 14/11/23. I had the pleasure this morning of meeting Mr A. de Brune the Sydney Daily Mail pedestrian, who is walking round Australia. I had a very interesting conversation with him and am quite satisfied that Australians generally do not know the conditions prevailing outback. Wishing Mr de Brune every success, yours faithfully, J. J. Angby.
Police Station, Georgetown, 14/11/23. I had the pleasure this date of having a conversation with Mr Aidan de Brune and am satisfied from my own personal knowledge of the Territory, travelled by our friend, that his experiences when reduced to book form and distributed among the rising generation, will be of the utmost educational value to Australia as a whole. W. H. Kitchen, police officer.

Having had the pleasure of meeting and listening to Mr de Brune's lecture on his walk around Australia, I feel deeply interested in the possibilities of our great island continent, and my great hope is that some statesman—not politician—may take notice of Mr de Brune's remarks relating to our great north, and then set to work to evolve a sound policy to develop the northern territory, so that it may be the supporting and not the depending part of Australia. Wishing Mr de Brune success and health during the rest of his walk around Australia, sincerely yours. A. Oliver Badman.
Mr de Brune rested at Yacka for one night. I wish him the best of luck on his journey. Francis L. Nykiel, Broughton Hotel, Yacka.

26 November 1923
Day 798 [789]
State or Territory: SA
Cumulative Days Walked: 498
Daily Distance (miles): 0
Cumulative Distance (miles): 8938
Note: At Adelaide.
Certification/Comment: Had a very interesting chat with Mr A. de Brune, who brought a letter of introduction from Mr E. J. MaCarthy, manager of Esperance Land Company, Mr de Brune having carried the letter on foot from Esperance—1588 miles. J. M. Genders, secretary.
I have had a short chat with Mr Aidan de Brune concerning his travels in Australia and native country (Canada), also respecting his visit to Esperance from where he has carried a letter to me from Mr E. J. McCarthy, manager of the company there. I wish him a pleasant journey to Sydney, where I understand this tour will end. C. J. Hargreaves, chairman, Esperance Land Co.
J. P. Basedow, M.D., Kent town, S.A.
Herald Office, Adelaide S.A., 26/1/23. Comrade de Brune called at the Herald office today. Looks fit. It's a pleasure to meet him. If he adheres to his present occupation, he need never be unemployed. The work is healthy and the result, if published, should be both interesting and educational. Australians know very little about their own country, and this Canadian should teach us something. H. Kneebone.
It was a pleasure to me to listen to Mr de Brune's experiences of his long walk round Australia, especially through that practically unexplored portion of the far north. Only one thoroughly acquainted with the Australian bush life and its customs could endure the great trials and hardships encountered on such a journey. I hope the knowledge gained on his long walk will result in bringing about better conditions for those living in that far outback region. Dudley E. Kelsay, hon. sec. N.T. Association.
27 November 1923
Day 799 [790]
State or Territory: SA
Cumulative Days Walked: 498
Daily Distance (miles): 0
Cumulative Distance (miles): 8938
Note: At Adelaide.
Certification/Comment: From F. P. Ward, Secretary, S.A. Branch, Australian Labor Party. Pleased to receive a visit from Aidan de Brune who is engaged in a walk around the coastline of Australia. Personally, I regard walking as a pleasure. Would sooner walk than ride in a motor car. Can understand, however, that in such a walk there would be many hardships. Very different to having meals at home. Hope to read the account of Mr de Brune's walk. Should be very interesting. Fred Ward.
I was very pleased to have the opportunity of hearing something of your very wonderful trip. Raymond L. Lean, Commissioner of Police, Adelaide. 27/11/23.

1/12/23. Ambleside, South Australia. The bearer of this most interesting diary, Mr Aidan de Brune, arrived here yesterday after a very long and tiresome journey, not showing the least signs of fatigue. The writer, having also visited very many parts in the far north-west of Western Australia, found that the traveller was most interesting. I also attended his lecture to a very full house. Wishing him all the success he deserves to get, on his unexpired journey. J. R. Lineham, Ambleside Hotel.

I have had the pleasure of presiding at a lecture by Mr de Brune on his trip around Australia, per boot. Information first-hand, given out tonight, must convince his audience of the capabilities and possibilities of the Northern Territory, for the peopling of the N.T. by whites—and the necessity of the North-South line, direct. I wish he may get through his trip safely and successfully. Albert E. W. Virgo, Bordertown. 14/12/23.

The information he will gather from his travel will eventually become an historic book and in future generations will adorn every bookshelf from Sydney round Australia. I wish him every success and trust he will reach his haven in safety, when I am sure he will be received with great pride. W. Wallace, postmaster. 15/12/23.

Have been pleased to meet Mr de Brune and to provide his Christmas dinner, Horsham, 25/12/23. It is an honour one seldom obtains. I wish him every luck and God speed on his remaining journey and the compliments of the season. W. Lloyd, Royal Hotel, Horsham.
Mr de Brune called on me at Horsham today. I was pleased to note his moral and physical vigour, and sincerely trust he will reach his destination safely and that the knowledge gained by him will be of financial benefit to himself and great value to the people of Australia. G. Germaine, Inspt. of Police. 25/12/23.
I am proud to say Mr de Brune stayed at my Hotel on Christmas night. I wish him every success and a prosperous new year. Thomas Doyle, Dooen Hotel, Dooen, via Horsham.

Certification/Comment: Stawell News Office, Main Street, Stawell, 28/12/23. I have had the pleasure today of meeting Mr Aidan de Brune, special reporter of Sydney Daily Mail. He has cut out a couple of records and I regret exceedingly that his itinerary will not permit him to give me more of his interesting experiences. He is a "God-send" to a newspaper in search of original copy. However, I wish Aidan de Brune a happy fulfilment of his self-imposed long and lonely trek and, though late in the day, the compliments of the season and good luck. Flitwood Smith, proprietor.

He stayed at my hotel last night and is now finishing his breakfast. Is prepared to take the dry and dusty road again and to complete his tramp around big Australia. Mr de Brune is not a very big man in build but has a very big heart to undertake such a hard and long tramp for the past two years and more. I wish him good luck and success, back to Sydney amongst his friends. Thomas Sawyer, Thirlmere.

Edward P. Kelsall, editor, Labor Daily.
I had the pleasure of meeting Mr de Brune at Darwin, N.T. He had then come through some terrible stages and knowing what was ahead of him, thought he was continuing a hopeless task. While in Darwin Mr de Brune endeavoured to reconcile industrial troubles, but failed by reason of the active efforts of certain Government officials, whose desire was to foment them. Aidan de Brune is one of the gamest men I have ever had the honour to know. J. T. Beckett, Labor Daily, 4/3/24.
I have followed the walk of Aidan de Brune with great interest and his powers of description and humour are all powerful. May his shadow never grow less. H. Barry, accountant, 4/3/24.
J. J. Gilchrist, Daily Mail, 4/3/24.
COMMENTS MADE IN THE DIARY FOLLOWING COMPLETION OF THE WALK
Certification/Comment: Trades Hall, Sydney, 7/3/24. Aidan de Brune visited my office today and, after hearing of his experiences, all I can say is that he has a bigger heart than me. Such spirits as he, do things. J. S. Garden.
Mr de Brune called at this office and delivered a letter, per foot, from Melbourne, and we are aware of the hardships he must have had during this walk which he did around Australia. Federated Liquor Union of Employees, F. Owen, Secretary.
Rexona Office. Was indeed glad to see you and learn Rexona had proved a good friend on your trip. Sincerely, Rexona, S.H.S.
I was glad to meet Mr de Brune when he called upon me today, after his wonderful trip of 10,000 miles around Australia. He has the heroic spirit that seemed to have vanished with the days of romance. Henry E. Boote, 10/3/24.
I was very pleased to have met Mr de Brune after his great feat in walking round Australia, and to receive from him a letter which he carried from Geraldton in W.A. to me, from Vic. Johnson.—E. Grayndler, Gen. Sec. A.W.U.
Who ever is this sunburned stranger? Ah, Mr Aidan de Brune. On this day, 9/3/24, Mr de Brune appeared on our doorstep, springing a surprise on all those dwelling within. We all spent a pleasant evening, thanks very much to Mr de Brune's beautiful playing.—Joan.
Mr W. Oliver, chairman, to Mr de Brune. Communist Hall, 23/3/24.
G. Edgecumbe, secretary, Australian Journalists Association, N.S.W. District. 17/4/24.
23/4/24. I think Mr de Brune's trip around Australia, on foot, only goes to show what Australians can do. L. E. Murnin, Press Club.
24/4/24. No one enjoyed Mr de Brune's articles on his trip round Australia more than I did. They were an education to us, tied to the city. E. J. Hill.
Mr de Brune ranks with our best and most intrepid explorers. W. J. O'Connelly, Sydney. 24/4/24.
I wish I had the opportunity of accompanying Mr de Brune on his trip round Australia. Con. Drew, 24/4/24.
F. A. Chaffey.
Such a trip around Australia should be an education to even the best of us, but I am afraid my education will have to be neglected from this point of view, unless I am provided with wheels. I'm afraid such a long arduous journey would try even the best motor car. Eric Bedford.
Stick to it, old man, and go to it. Good luck, and don't forget to punch all land huggers hard. Release the big lands and Aussie is on the pig's back. J.L.B.
Aidan de Brune,/A Champion Walker,/A good sport,/An excellent talker. J. N. Rogers, Labor Daily. 15/5/24.
A famous streamline on the Daily Mail front page: With sighs and groans, Aidan de Brune struggles on. G. W. Warnecke.
An appreciation of a wonderful walk under the auspices of the Daily Mail. R. N. Connolly.
Yet another appreciation—of your keen journalism after the walk. C. O'Sullivan, 1/9/24.
Aidan de Brune walks into Darwin and settles a strike. Another Daily Mail heading. One of the stories chronicling a remarkable walk. G. E. Kelly.
Commiseration for one of the worst treated men that ever walked, Aidan de Brune.—Chas. A. Lee.

STATISTICS FOR THE WALK

These statistics have been complied from totals appearing in the typescript of Record Journal of a Walk Around Australia, although they did not appear in the format presented here. The mileage walked each day was entered into a spreadsheet. From these figures the total miles walked, total for each state/territory, cumulative mileage at the end of each day, and number of days on which he did not walk, were calculated.

De Brune was remarkably accurate in his arithmetic. A few non-material errors were made which, in total, had virtually no effect. As mentioned in chapter 4, he was as accurate as he could be with distances. In many cases he had to use his best guess to calculate the distance travelled in a day. No doubt he was careful to check his distances with the overall distance between points, distances which he found on sign posts, along railways lines or telegraph lines, or on maps. Whatever the distance he travelled, his was an epic walk. Let us not be churlish in allowing him to describe it as a walk of "ten thousand miles."

A Walk Around Australia by Aidan de Brune NSW-North QLD NT WA SA VIC NSW-South
Date started in State 20/09/1921 15/10/1921 20/05/1922 02/10/1922 23/09/1923 17/12/1923 04/02/1924
Date ended in State 14/10/1921 19/05/1922 01/10/1922 22/09/1923 16/12/1923 03/02/1924 04/03/1924
Distance for State (miles) 492 2218 1519 3849 1059 533 390
Total number of days 25 217 135 356 85 49 30
Days lost due to sickness and delays 6 92 44 137 22 19 5
Days walked 19 125 91 219 63 30 25
